complete pipeline of how a CSS style change triggers layout and paint in the Firefox/Gecko browser engine.\\n\\n### 1. Style Change Notification\\n\\nThe process begins when a style change is detected (via attribute changes, class changes, or direct style modifications):\\n\\n- **Entry Point**: `layout/base/nsLayoutUtils.cpp:PostRestyleEvent()` - This is the public API that posts restyle events for elements that have changed style.\\n- **Core Handler**: `layout/style/RestyleManager.h` and `layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp` - The RestyleManager class is responsible for managing the restyling process. It receives change notifications through `PostRestyleEvent(Element*, RestyleHint, nsChangeHint)`.\\n- **Context**: `layout/base/nsPresContext.h` and `.cpp` - The nsPresContext owns the RestyleManager and coordinates the overall presentation.\\n\\n### 2. Frame Style Recomputation\\n\\nOnce restyle events are posted, they are processed during a flush:\\n\\n- **Style Computation**: `layout/style/ServoStyleSet.h` and `layout/style/ServoStyleSet.cpp` - ServoStyleSet performs the actual style computation using the Servo CSS engine. It computes new styles for elements based on CSS rules and cascade.\\n- **Gecko Bindings**: `layout/style/GeckoBindings.cpp` - Bridges between the Servo style engine and Gecko layout code. Functions like `Gecko_ElementStateChanged()` notify Gecko when element state changes require restyling.\\n- **Change Hints**: `layout/style/nsChangeHint.h` - Defines nsChangeHint flags that specify what layout work is needed (reflow, repaint, etc.) based on the style change.\\n- **Restyle State**: The `ServoRestyleState` class in `layout/style/RestyleManager.h` manages the state during the restyle traversal, including tracking which frames need work.\\n\\n### 3. Dirty Frame Reflow Scheduling\\n\\nAfter styles are recomputed, frames are marked dirty and reflow is scheduled:\\n\\n- **Restyle Processing**: `layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp:ProcessRestyledFrames()` - This function processes the list of elements that were restyled, examines their change hints, and marks frames dirty accordingly. It iterates through the style change list and applies the necessary frame updates.\\n- **Frame Marking**: `layout/base/PresShell.h` and `layout/base/PresShell.cpp:FrameNeedsReflow()` - This method marks a frame and its ancestors as needing reflow by setting dirty bits (NS_FRAME_IS_DIRTY, NS_FRAME_HAS_DIRTY_CHILDREN). It also adds the frame to the dirty roots list for reflow scheduling.\\n- **Reflow Scheduling**: `layout/generic/nsIFrame.h` - The nsIFrame base class manages frame state bits that track dirty status. Ancestors are marked with NS_FRAME_HAS_DIRTY_CHILDREN to propagate the need for reflow up the tree.\\n- **Flush Mechanism**: `layout/base/PresShell.cpp:FlushPendingNotifications()` and `DoFlushPendingNotifications()` - These methods coordinate the flushing of different types of pending notifications (style, frames, layout). They ensure the restyle and reflow happen in the correct order.\\n\\n### 4. Display List Construction\\n\\nDuring reflow, the display list is rebuilt to represent what needs to be painted:\\n\\n- **Reflow Execution**: `layout/base/PresShell.cpp:DoReflow()` - Performs the actual reflow by calling frame's Reflow() methods. This recalculates sizes and positions.\\n- **Display List Building**: `layout/painting/nsDisplayList.h` and `layout/painting/nsDisplayList.cpp:nsDisplayListBuilder` - The nsDisplayListBuilder constructs the display list by traversing the frame tree. It builds display items that represent visual content in z-order.\\n- **Frame Traversal**: Frames' `BuildDisplayList()` methods are called recursively to build display items. Each frame contributes its own display items (backgrounds, borders, content, etc.).\\n- **Retained Display Lists**: `layout/painting/RetainedDisplayListBuilder.h` and `layout/painting/RetainedDisplayListBuilder.cpp` - Optimizes display list building by retaining and reusing parts of the previous display list when possible, only rebuilding changed portions.\\n- **Display List Processing**: The built display list is then used for painting. It contains all the visual elements in the correct z-order and clipping information needed for rendering.\\n\\n### 5. WebRender Layer Update\\n\\nFinally, the display list is converted to WebRender commands for GPU-accelerated rendering:\\n\\n- **Layer Manager**: `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderLayerManager.h` and `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderLayerManager.cpp` - The WebRenderLayerManager is the compositor abstraction that manages the rendering pipeline. It converts the display list into WebRender display list format.\\n- **State Management**: `gfx/layers/wr/RenderRootStateManager.h` - Manages the WebRender state for a render root, handling display items and WebRender commands.\\n- **Bridge Communication**: `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderBridgeChild.h` and `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderBridgeChild.cpp` - Communicates with the WebRender bridge parent process, sending the display list and resource updates.\\n- **Transaction**: The display list is wrapped in a WebRender transaction that updates the WebRender scene. This includes creating WebRender display list items, handling scrolling data, and managing layer properties.\\n- **GPU Rendering**: WebRender processes these commands on the GPU, performing composition, rasterization, and other rendering operations.\\n\\n### Summary of the Chain\\n\\nThe complete flow is:\\n\\n1. Style change detected → **PostRestyleEvent()** (nsLayoutUtils, RestyleManager)\\n2. Style recomputed → **ServoStyleSet** processes styles, determines **nsChangeHint**\\n3.
